Title: Affine Springer fiber and the small quantum group

URL Source: https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.11966v1

Published Time: Wed, 15 Apr 2026 00:06:58 GMT

Number of Pages: 83

Markdown Content:
AFFINE SPRINGER FIBER AND THE SMALL QUANTUM GROUP 

ROMAN BEZRUKAVNIKOV, PABLO BOIXEDA ALVAREZ, MICHAEL MCBREEN, AND ZHIWEI YUN 

Abstract. We find a new geometric incarnation for the principal block in the category of modules over a quantum group at a root of unity, realizing it as a full subcategory of microsheaves on a certain affine Springer fiber. We also prove a related geometric Langlands type equivalence with wild ramification, identifying the latter category with a category of coherent sheaves on the Springer resolution for the dual group. This can also be viewed as a version of homological mirror symmetry for the Springer resolution. 

Contents

The results of this article have several sources of motivation belonging, respectively, to representation theory, geometric Langlands duality and homological mirror symmetry. From the representation theory perspective, the main result (see Theorem 1.1.4) is a new geometric realization of a category of modules over the quantum group at a root of unity. Earlier theorems of this nature identified a category of quantum group modules with perverse sheaves on the affine or semi-infinite flag manifold, which implies the relation between the appropriate version of the affine Kazhdan-Lusztig polynomials to numerical invariants of representations. Theorem 1.1.4 below relates quantum group modules to a different geometric object: it asserts its equivalence with a full subcategory PŌą of 

microsheaves on a certain affine Springer fiber Fl Ōą , where Ōą = tŌą 1 ‚ąą g(( t)) and Ōą1 ‚ąą g is regular semisimple; or more precisely, microsheaves on a certain symplectic variety MŌą supported on a conical Lagrangian subset homeomorphic to Fl Ōą . The known and expected applications (see [23] and Theorem 1.3.2 below) are also different. The category PŌą of microsheaves on Fl Ōą also admits a description in terms of perverse sheaves: it turns out to be equivalent to a full subcategory in the category of perverse sheaves on the affine flag variety Fl of G, Whittaker-equivariant with respect to the first congruence subgroup G[t‚ąí1]1 in the group of negative loops G[t‚ąí1] equipped with the additive character given by Ōą; the space MŌą above is the shifted

Hamiltonian reduction of T ‚ąóFl by the action of G[t‚ąí1]1 (by a shifted Hamiltonian reduction we understand the quotient of the preimage of dŌą = Ōą1dt under the moment map). We believe that the microlocal description of the category of (partially) Whittaker sheaves is a general phenomenon with strong potential applications in representation theory, see 1.4.4 below. To make sense of Whittaker sheaves in an arbitrary sheaf-theoretic context (without necessarily the Artin-Schreier sheaves or exponential D-modules at our disposal), we use the notion of Kirillov category introduced by Gaitsgory [26]. The quotient of the affine flag variety by the congruence subgroup G[t‚ąí1]1 is the moduli stack of G-bundles on P1 with level structures at zero and infinity, so the study of sheaves on this space belongs in geometric Langlands duality. Accordingly, we establish an equivalence (see Theorem 1.1.3) between the derived category of microsheaves and the derived category of coherent sheaves on a stack of Langlands parameters which can be identified with the derived category of quantum group modules based on [2] and [48]. On the other hand, we can also realize the symplectic variety MŌą as the moduli space of Higgs bundles on P1 with a regular singularities at zero and an irregular one at infinity (of order 2), as explained in [9]. There is a corresponding Betti space MBet ,Ōą , diffeomorphic to a quotient of MŌą by an action of the lattice 

X‚ąó(T ) of cocharacters of a maximal torus T ‚äā G. The space MBet ,Ōą is (for suitable choices of parameters) a smooth affine variety of finite type, and thus comes equipped with a contractible space of Weinstein structures. Microsheaves on MBet ,Ōą may be identified with a version of the Fukaya category, using the general theory developed in [29]. One expects that the category of microsheaves on MŌą is equivalent to a suitable X‚ąó(T )-graded version of the Fukaya category of MBet ,Ōą .Combining the above discussions with the geometric Langlands type equivalence in Theorem 1.1.3, one would thus establish homological mirror symmetry (HMS) between MBet ,Ōą and a space of Langlands parameters. While this case of HMS was among our sources of motivation, we do not work with Fukaya categories in this paper, thus this statement remains conjectural. 1.1. Kirillov category and microsheaves on the affine Springer fiber. 

1.1.1. Affine Springer fiber. Let G be a connected reductive group over C with Lie algebra g. Let C(( t)) be the field of Laurent series in one variable t, and let G(( t)) be the associated loop group with Lie algebra 

g(( t)) = g ‚äóC C(( t)). Let I ‚äā G(( t)) be an Iwahori subgroup. Let Ōą1 ‚ąą g be regular semisimple and 

Ōą = tŌą 1 ‚ąą g(( t)). We denote by Fl Ōą = {g ‚ąą G(( t)) /I|Ad( g‚ąí1Ōą ‚ąą Lie I)} the affine Springer fiber of Ōą in the affine flag variety Fl = G(( t)) /I. Note that Fl Ōą has irreducible components in bijection with the extended affine Weyl group fW = X‚ąó(T ) ‚čä W , and each component has dimension equal to that of the flag variety 

B of G (in fact some components can be identified with B). It also carries a Gm-action given by loop rotation (scaling t). Just as the usual Springer fibers, the affine Springer fiber Fl Ōą can be embedded into a symplectic variety 

MŌą as a Lagrangian. Moreover, the Gm-action on Fl Ōą extends to MŌą , and all points of MŌą contracts to points in Fl Ōą under this action. This is not a general structure for any affine Springer fiber but crucially relies on the Gm-symmetry on Fl Ōą . A more general construction of this kind is done in our previous paper [9]. 1.1.2. Kirillov category. In geometric representation theory we often encounter sheaf-theoretic versions of Whittaker models whose definition involves an Artin-Schreier sheaf on the affine line, so a priori only makes sense over a characteristic p base field, or in the context of D-modules where we replace Artin-Schreier sheaf by the exponential D-module. Gaitsgory [26] gives a way to define such geometric Whittaker categories in any sheaf-theoretic context (in particular in the Betti setting), when the Ga-action on the space involved extends to an action of Ga ‚čä G m (where Gm acts on Ga by scaling). 1.2. Microsheaves and microlocal fiber functor for Satake category. As mentioned in the begin-ning, DŌą is an incarnation of a category of microsheaves on Fl Ōą in the classical sheaf-theoretic context. We now make this statement more precise. Following Nadler and Shende [42, 43], we consider the category őľSh Fl Ōą (MŌą ) of microsheaves on MŌą

supported on Fl Ōą . More details on microsheaves will be recalled in ¬ß3.1 and ¬ß4.7. Let őľSh Fl Ōą ,f s (MŌą )be the full subcategory of őľSh Fl Ōą (MŌą ) consisting of microsheaves supported on finitely many irreducible components of Fl Ōą and with cohomologically bounded and finite-dimensional microstalks. A general construction for Kirillov categories provides a microlocalization functor 

fM : eDŌą ‚Üí őľSh( MŌą ).

1.2.1. Theorem (See Theorem 7.5.4 and Proposition 7.6.2) . The functor fM restricts to a full embedding of categories 

(1.2) M : DŌą ,‚Üí őľSh Fl Ōą ,f s (MŌą ).

Consequences of theorems in ¬ß1.1 at the level of Grothendieck groups are used in the recent work of Feng-Le Hung [23] that solves cases of the Breuil-M¬ī ezard conjecture on the deformation space of Galois representations. with slope of the form 1 /m .1.4.4. Microsheaves on usual Springer fibers. Let e be a nilpotent element in g, Se ‚äā N be the (nilpotent part of the) Slodowy slice through e and eSe be the preimage of Se under the Springer resolution. Then the Springer fiber Be is a conical Lagrangian in eSe, and we may consider the category of microsheaves 

őľSh Be ( eSe). Our construction in this paper suggests a sheaf-theoretic model for őľSh Be ( eSe), namely a full subcategory in the category Kir( Ve\B ), where Ve is the kernel of the character Ōąe : Ue ‚Üí Ga for a Premet subgroup Ue and its character Ōąe whose differential equals the linear functional defined by e. For example, if e is even and {e, h, f } is an sl 2-triple, then Lie Ue is the sum of negative weight spaces of g under h. We expect this category to be equivalent to the category of finite dimensional modules over the corresponding 

W -algebra with an integral regular central character. Notice that this category is closely connected to the D-modules (or Harish-Chandra bimodules) realization of the asymptotic Hecke category [37] and to character D-modules [13]. We expect the above topological realization to yield a generalization of these results to the constructible setting. 1.4.5. Characteristic p version. We expect that our results can be extended to the setting when the coefficient field E has positive characteristic. The analogue of Theorem 1.1.4 is a Koszul duality between the category of microsheaves and a regular block in the category of ( G‚ą® 

> 1

, T ‚ą®)-modules where G‚ą® 

> 1

is the kernel of the Frobenius morphism for the reductive group G‚ą® over E. Notice that a key ingredient in the proof of Theorem 1.1.4, the relation of modules over the Lusztig quantum group and perverse sheaves on the affine Grassmannian [2] has a positive characteristic analogue known as the Finkelberg‚ÄďMirkovi¬ī cconjecture, which was established in [18] with some restrictions on char( E). However, the proof of Theorem 1.1.4 relies also on the formality from weights argument which is not available in positive characteristic, thus the generalization requires a different technical implementation of the strategy outlined in Remark 8.1.2. 6 ROMAN BEZRUKAVNIKOV, PABLO BOIXEDA ALVAREZ, MICHAEL MCBREEN, AND ZHIWEI YUN 

1.4.6. Coherent duality for affine Springer fibers. We briefly describe a heuristic relation of our results and the more general [9, Conjecture 1.4.1] to the conjectural equivalence between two coherent categorifications of the double affine Hecke algebra (DAHA), which is a local counterpart of the classical limit of the geometric Langlands duality. Varagnolo and Vasserot [49, Theorem 2.5.6] introduced a categorification of DAHA coming from the derived category of equivariant coherent sheaves on the loop group analogue of the Steinberg variety (a similar construction for the spherical, degenerate DAHA appeared in [12]). One expects that the monoidal categories constructed this way from two Langlands dual group G, G‚ą® are naturally equivalent, see [12, 

¬ß7.9] for the similar conjecture in the spherical case. Next, this equivalence of monoidal categories should come with compatible equivalence of module categories as follows. We fix an invariant quadratic form yielding a vector space isomorphism t ‚ąľ= t‚ą® and an isomorphism of Chevalley spaces t/W ‚ąľ= t‚ą®/W . Let e ‚ąą ő≥(( t)) and e‚ą® ‚ąą ő≥‚ą®(( t)) be regular semisimple topologically nilpotent elements whose images in the Chevalley space match under this isomorphism. Then one expects an equivalence 

DCoh (Fl e) ‚ąľ= DCoh Ze‚ą® (Fl e‚ą® )where Ze‚ą® is the centralizer of e‚ą® and Fl e, Fl e‚ą® are the affine Springer fibers; (1.4.6) should be an equivalence of module categories over the two coherent categorifications of DAHA. The heuristic of S1-localization proposed by Ben-Zvi and Nadler [5] suggests that (1.4.6) should imply another equivalence of categories obtained, respectively, from the left hand side by quantization and from the right hand side by passing to the similar object for the finite dimensional group G‚ą® replacing the corresponding loop group. In the special case when e = ts as above, the two categories can be arguable identified with the two sided of the equivalence in Theorem 1.1.3. 1.5. Notation and convention. 

1.5.1. Sheaf-theoretic contexts. Let X be an algebraic stack of finite type over an algebraically closed field 

k. Let E be a field of characteristic zero depending on the sheaf-theoretic context. We will use the notation 

D(X) to denote any of the following E-linear sheaf-theoretic categories in different contexts:

‚ÄĘ Betti: k = C and E is any field of characteristic zero field. We take D(X) to be the bounded derived category of constructible sheaves on X with E-coefficients for the classical topology on 

X(C).

D-modules on X.The main body of the paper is written in the ¬ī etale context, although all arguments in the paper work for the Betti and de Rham contexts equally well. 1.5.2. Half Tate twist. In the ¬ī etale setting, we have Tate twist as a local system on Spec k

Acknowledgements 

The authors would like to thank Tony Feng and Ben Gammage for stimulating conversations. 2. Kirillov category 

We elaborate on Gaitsgory‚Äôs construction of the Kirillov category, which will serve as a model in the usual sheaf-theoretic context for talking about microsheaves. We also give an alternative construction of the Kirillov category in ¬ß2.3 that is more flexible for applications. We will freely use material about monodromic sheaves such as monodromic vanishing cycles and mon-odromic Fourier transform, which are reviewed and further developed in Appendix A. 2.1. Kirillov category after Gaitsgory [26] . Let Aff = Ga ‚čä G m be the group of affine transformations of A1. Let X be a stack with an action of Aff. 2.1.1. Definition. The Kirillov category for the stack X with Aff-action is the quotient Kir( X) = DGm (X)/D Aff (X)under the forgetful functor DAff (X) ,‚Üí DGm (X). 2.3. Alternative construction. We give an alternative construction of the Kirillov category that makes certain symmetries more transparent. The setup is the same as ¬ß2.1. This construction is only used in the rest of paper to make sense of integral transforms on Kirillov categories given by kernel sheaves that are 

Ga-equivariant and Gm-monodromic (as opposed to Gm-equivariant), see ¬ß2.3.9. Such integral transforms will allow us to define Hecke symmetries on automorphic Kirillov categories (see ¬ß6.4 and ¬ß7.1.4). In this subsection alone, we work with cocomplete versions of sheaf categories (ind-constructible sheaves). 2.3.1. Monodromic category. Let DGm-mon (X) ‚äā D(X) be the full subcategory generated by the image of DGm (X) under the forgetful functor, i.e., unipotently monodromic complexes. 3. Recollections on microsheaves 

In this section we assume the base field k = C, and work with the analytic topology on various smooth complex varieties. We will review the basics of microsheaves, and recall a few properties which we will have use for later, as well as some general context and motivation. None of this material is original. 3.1. Microsheaves. 16 ROMAN BEZRUKAVNIKOV, PABLO BOIXEDA ALVAREZ, MICHAEL MCBREEN, AND ZHIWEI YUN 

3.1.1. Microsheaves on cotangent bundles. We follow [32] and [42] to recall the formalism of microsheaves. Let N be a smooth complex manifold, and let Sh( N ) be the dg category of unbounded complexes of sheaves on N . For any subset őõ ‚äā T ‚ąóN , let Sh őõ(N ) be the full subcategory of sheaves with singular support contained in őõ. For an open subset ő© ‚äā T ‚ąóN (with respect to the usual topology on a complex manifold), let Sh( N ; ő©) be the quotient Sh( N )/Sh T ‚ąóN ‚ąíő©(N ). The assignment őľSh pre : ő© 7 ‚Üí Sh( N ; ő©) is a presheaf of stable ‚ąě-categories. Let ő© 7 ‚Üí őľSh(ő©) be the sheafification of őľSh pre . It is a sheaf of stable 

‚ąě-categories. For any open ő© ‚äā T ‚ąóN , an object F ‚ąą őľSh(ő©) has a well-defined singular support SS (F), which is a conical subset in ő©. For a subset őõ ‚äā T ‚ąóN and open ő© ‚äā T ‚ąóN , we let őľSh őõ(ő©) denote the category of sections of őľSh(ő©) with singular support in őõ ‚ą© ő©. For F, G ‚ąą Sh( N ), in [32] a complex of sheaves őľhom( F, G) on T ‚ąóN is defined. We have Hom őľSh(ő©) (F, G) = H 0(ő© , őľ hom( F, G)) .

The support of őľhom( F, G) is contained in SS (F) ‚ą© SS (G). 3.1.2. Extension to stacks. We refer to [43, Section 4] for more details on microsheaves on a stack. We will only need the case of a global quotient X = [ N/G ] where N is a smooth scheme over C. In this case, 

T ‚ąóX = [ őľ‚ąí1(0) /G ] where őľ : T ‚ąóN ‚Üí g‚ąó is the moment map for the G-action on N . For ő© ‚äā őľ‚ąí1(0) that is G-invariant, we can still form őľSh pre (ő© /G ) := Sh( X)/Sh őľ‚ąí1(0) ‚ąíő©(X). 3.1.3. Definition. Define a sheaf of stable ‚ąě-categories őľSh over the stack T ‚ąóX by sheafifying the above presheaf. We denote its global section category by őľSh( T ‚ąóX) = őľSh( őľ‚ąí1(0) /G ). 3.1.4. Microsheaves on exact symplectic manifolds. An exact sympectic manifold is a (smooth, real) man-ifold X equipped with a real one-form őĽ, such that ŌČ = dőĽ is a symplectic form. The image of őĽ under the isomorphism of vector bundles T ‚ąóX ‚Üí T X defined by ŌČ is called the Liouville vector-field. The flow of this vector field is called the Liouville flow. 3.1.5. Example. Let N be a manifold, and let X = T ‚ąóN be equipped with the usual symplectic structure. The action of R>0 dilating the cotangent fibers is the Liouville flow for the canonical Liouville form, which we denote őĽN .Exact symplectic manifolds bear a close relation to contact manifolds. To an exact symplectic manifold (X, őĽ ), we associate the contact manifold ( Y, őĪ ) = ( X √ó R, őĽ + dt ). 2

We will consider contact manifolds ( Y, őĪ ) and symplectic manifolds ( X, ŌČ ) equipped with an extra structure called Maslov data . This structure endows them with sheaves of categories locally modeled on the microsheaf categories defined by by Kashiwara and Schapira in [32]. We briefly sketch the definition of Maslov data below; a good reference for this material is [21, Section 3]. 3.1.6. Remark. We will use the same notation őľSh, and the same word microsheaves, for the sheaves of categories on a contact or symplectic manifold. As we recall below, there is a simple relationship between the two, and in practice this should not cause any confusion. Let C be a stable presentable symmetric monoidal category (eventually, this will be the category of coefficients for our microsheaves, and we may take it to be dg Z-modules or dg C-vector spaces). 3.1.7. Definition. Let ( X, ŌČ ) be a real symplectic manifold. There is a canonical sequence of maps (3.1) X ‚Üí B U ‚Üí B(U / O) ‚Üí B2 Pic( C)where the first map classifies the stable tangent bundle to X (viewed as a symplectic bundle), the second map is the delooping of the quotient map U ‚Üí U / O, and the last map is induced by a de-looping of the 

J-homomorphism. Maslov data for ( X, őĽ ) is a choice of null-homotopy of the resulting map X ‚Üí B2 Pic( C). We will denote such a choice of nullhomotopy by the variable ő∑ below.  

> 2One can also build a symplectic manifold from a contact manifold, though we will not need to do so here. AFFINE SPRINGER FIBER AND THE SMALL QUANTUM GROUP 17

3.1.8. Example. When C = Z ‚ąí mod, B 2 Pic( C) is given by B 2(Z) ‚äē B3(Z/2Z). A choice of Maslov data is canonically identified with a choice of trivialization of the complex line bundle det( TCX)‚äó2 and a class in H2(X, Z/2Z). Maslov data over other commutative rings R can then be obtained by composition with Pic( Z‚ąímod) ‚Üí

Pic( R ‚ąí mod). Maslov data for contact manifolds is defined similarly to the symplectic case, where the contact distri-bution plays the role of the tangent bundle. In particular, Maslov data for an exact symplectic manifold (X, őĽ ) determines Maslov data for ( X √ó R, őĽ + dt ). One natural way of producing Maslov data is as follows. 3.1.9. Definition. A stable polarization of X is a section of the Lagrangian Grassmanian bundle LGr( T X ‚äē

R2n) ‚Üí X for some n ‚Č• 0. We consider stable polarizations up to homotopy: they are classified by null-homotopies of the compo-sition (3.2) X ‚Üí B U ‚Üí B(U / O) of the first two maps in Equation 3.1. A choice of stable polarization defines Maslov data for X by composition. 3.1.10. Example. If X = T ‚ąóN is a cotangent bundle, then it carries a natural polarization, and thus natural Maslov data, which we denote ő∑N . Similarly, if Y = S‚ąóN is the cosphere bundle of a manifold N ,equipped with the canonical contact form őĪN , then it carries a natural (contact) polarization, and thus natural Maslov data, which we also denote ő∑N .The papers [47] and [42, Theorem 1.1] endow any contact manifold ( Y, őĪ ) equipped with a choice of Maslov data ( Y, őĪ, ő∑ ) with a sheaf of categories őľSh, which we call microsheaves. Suppose ( Y, őĪ, ő∑ ) = ( S‚ąóRn, őĪ N , ő∑ N ). Then the stalk of this sheaf at p ‚ąą S‚ąóRn is the category (3.3) Sh( Rn)/Sh S‚ąó\p(Rn),

where Sh( Rn) denotes sheaves on Rn with coefficients in C. This is essentially the category defined by Kashiwara and Schapira in [32], except that one works here with coefficients in a presentable category, rather than with bounded complexes. The same is true, non-canonically, for general ( Y, őĪ, ő∑ ). Any homotopy of Maslov data ő∑ ‚Üí ő∑‚Ä≤ induces an isomorphism on microsheaves. On the other hand, by the contact version of Darboux‚Äôs theorem, ( Y, őĪ )is locally isomorphic, as a contact manifold, to the cosphere bundle S‚ąóRn of a vector space. Thus the sheaf őľSh is always locally isomorphic to (3.3). 3.1.11. Definition. Given an exact symplectic manifold equipped with a choice of Maslov data ( X, őĽ, ő∑ ), we consider the associated contact manifold ( X √ó R, őĽ + dt, ő∑ ) equipped with the induced Maslov data. We then define őľSh on X as the pullback of őľSh on X √óR along the natural embedding i0 : X ‚Üí X √ó0 ‚äā X √óR.We call an object of őľSh( X) a microsheaf .3.1.12. Proposition. The support of a microsheaf is a closed coisotropic subset of X stable under the Liouville flow. 

Given any subset S ‚äā X, we can consider the subsheaf őľSh S ‚äā őľSh of objects supported on S.3.1.13. Remark. One could also pull back őľSh on X √ó R along the graph of any function f : X ‚Üí R; this corresponds to shifting the Liouville form by df .3.1.14. Remark. The dependence of őľSh on the Maslov data ő∑ is mild: any isotopy ő∑ ‚Üí ő∑‚Ä≤ induces an equivalence on microsheaves. 3.1.18. Objects from smooth lagrangians. 

3.1.19. Definition. Let ( X, őĽ, ő∑ ) be an exact symplectic manifold equipped with Maslov data. Let L ‚äā X

The condition őĽ|L = 0 can be relaxed to őĽ|L = df under certain conditions : see Theorem 3.2.4. 3.2. Microsheaves and Fukaya categories. In this section, we recall the relationship between mi-crosheaves and the Fukaya category. This material is motivational, and will not be used anywhere else in this paper. An exact symplectic manifold X is called Liouville if the Liouville flow is complete, and X is convex, in the sense that it admits an exhaustion {Xk ‚äā X|k ‚ąą N} by compact submanifolds with boundaries, such that the Liouville vector field is outward pointing along each boundary. We call such a pair ( Xk, őĽ )a Liouville domain .3.2.1. Definition. The core c(X, őĽ ) ‚äā X (sometimes called the skeleton) of a Liouville manifold ( X, őĽ ) is the maximal flow-invariant subset of Xk (for k ‚Čę 0) which is disjoint from ‚ąāX k.This does not depend on the choice of exhaustion. The core is a compact subset of X.3.2.2. Proposition. Any compactly supported object in őľSh( X) is supported in c(X, őĽ ).

3.2.3. Definition. Let Sh (X, őĽ ) = őľSh c(X,őĽ )(X, őĽ ). A Liouville form őĽ is sufficiently Weinstein if c(X, őĽ ) is sufficiently isotropic [43, Definition 9.10]. This holds, for example, if it is Whitney-stratified by isotropic submanifolds. There is a corresponding notion of sufficiently Weinstein homotopies between sufficiently Weinstein Liouville manifolds. It is proven in [43] that a sufficiently Weinstein homotopy őĽ ‚Üí őĽ‚Ä≤ induces an equivalence of Sh (X, őĽ )with Sh (X, őĽ ‚Ä≤). One consequence of this is the following. 3.2.4. Theorem. [43, Theorem 1.2] Let L be a compact exact Lagrangian submanifold of the sufficiently Weinstein manifold (X, őĽ, ő∑ ), equipped with secondary Maslov data. There is a fully faithful functor 

Loc( L) ‚Üí Sh (X, őĽ ).

3.2.5. Theorem. [29, Theorem 1.4] Let (X, őĽ, ő∑ ) be a Liouville manifold admitting homological cocores. 3

Let Sh (X, őĽ )c denote the category of compact objects. Then there is a canonical equivalence of dg categories 

Sh (X, őĽ )c ‚ąľ= Perf W(X, őĽ )op 

where Perf W(X, őĽ ) is the (opposite) category of the idempotent-completed pre-triangulated closure of the wrapped Fukaya category of X.

4. Affine Springer fiber and Hitchin moduli space 

Let k be an algebraically closed field. 4.1. Homogeneous affine Springer fiber with slope one. Let G be a connected reductive group over

There is an action of Gm on MŌą by simultaneously scaling the Higgs field and rotating 

P1. We take the inverse of the second action so that Ōą1dt is invariant under Gm. The induced action on 

AŌą is contracting to aŌą .The basic geometric properties of MŌą is summarized below. 4.3.3. Proposition ([9, Theorem 2.8.1, Lemma 2.15.6]) . (1) The stack MŌą is a smooth algebraic space locally of finite type over k of dimension |ő¶| (the number of roots of G). 

(2) The space MŌą carries a canonical symplectic structure with weight 1 under the Gm-action. 

(3) The map fŌą is a completely integrable system. In particular, fibers of fŌą are Lagrangians in MŌą .

(4) For any őĺ ‚ąą M Ōą , the limit point lim s‚Üí0 s ¬∑ őĺ under the Gm-action exists.

Any compactly supported object in őľSh( MŌą , őĽ ) is supported on a finite union of irreducible components of the central Hitchin fiber őõŌą ‚äā M Ōą .Proof. The support of any such object is conical with respect to the Liouville flow. Any compact conical subset must be contained in őõ Ōą . Since the support is coisotropic, it must be a union of irreducible components of őõ Ōą . ‚Ė°26 ROMAN BEZRUKAVNIKOV, PABLO BOIXEDA ALVAREZ, MICHAEL MCBREEN, AND ZHIWEI YUN 

For this and other reasons (see the discussion of Fukaya categories below), it is natural to restrict our attention to the subcategory őľSh őõŌą (MŌą , őĽ ) of microlocal sheaves supported on őõ Ōą . We also sometimes abuse notation and write this as őľSh Fl Ōą (MŌą , őĽ ). 4.7.3. Lattice action. The action of the lattice X‚ąó(T ) on MŌą does not commute with the action of C‚ąó,and in particular does not preserve the one-form őĽ and does not map conical subsets of MŌą to conical subsets. For the same reason, the lattice does not act on the category őľSh( MŌą , őĽ ). However, X‚ąó(T ) does preserve the subset őõ Ōą , and we expect that it acts on őľSh őõŌą (MŌą , őĽ ) by automorphisms. Indeed, for each 

ŌÉ ‚ąą X‚ąó(T ), one may pick a homotopy between ŌÉ‚ąóőĽ and őĽ such that őõ Ōą is fiberwise conical. We expect that these homotopies, composed with the translation action of ŌÉ ‚ąą X‚ąó(T ) induce an action of X‚ąó(T ) on 

őľSh őõŌą (MŌą , őĽ ), following the construction in [42]. We will not use this action in the present paper. It should be the microlocal counterpart of the action defined in Section 6.2. 4.8. Speculations on Fukaya categories. We now turn to the question of associating a Fukaya category to the space MŌą . The form őĽ does not make MŌą into a Liouville manifold, because MŌą is not of finite type. There are various methods available to try and circumvent this problem; we sketch two approaches here. 4.8.1. Via localization to the core. Recall the Hitchin map f : MŌą ‚Üí A Ōą . Fix a linear metric on AŌą , and consider the family of balls Bk ‚äā A Ōą of radius k > 0 centered at aŌą . Set MkŌą = f ‚ąí1(Bk) ‚äā M Ōą . Then the flow of the vector field associated to őĽ is outward pointing along ‚ąāMkŌą . The core of ( MŌą , őĽ ) may be defined as in Definition 3.2.1, where we set Xk = MkŌą .4.8.2. Lemma. The core of MŌą is the central fiber of the Hitchin fibration: c(MŌą , őĽ ) = őõ Ōą .Proof. The Liouville vector field dilates AŌą , with unique fixed point aŌą . Hence c(MŌą , őĽ ) ‚äā f ‚ąí1(aŌą ) = őõ Ōą .The opposite containment follows from the fact that őõ Ōą is a union of compact conical subsets. ‚Ė°

The fact that the core őõ Ōą is ind-compact is a clue that ( MŌą , őĽ ) in many respects behaves like a finite type Liouville manifold. For instance, the statement of Theorem 3.2.4 should hold for ( MŌą , őĽ ). We may then seek to define the Fukaya category in terms of Sh (X, őĽ ) := őľSh őõŌą (MŌą , őĽ ), converting Theorem 3.2.5 into a definition. 4.8.3. Via the lattice quotient. A natural approach to producing a (finite type) Liouville manifold from 

MŌą is to take a quotient by the action of the lattice X‚ąó(T ), which preserves the symplectic form and the subset őõ Ōą . The lattice action is free and discontinuous on őõ Ōą ‚äā M Ōą , and the quotient őõ Ōą /X‚ąó(T ) is of finite type. The same should be true of a small tubular neighborhood of őõ Ōą .4.8.4. Definition. Fix a small ball BŌĶ ‚äā A Ōą centered at aŌą , and let YŌą = f ‚ąí1(BŌĶ)/X‚ąó(T ). The space YŌą is a finite type manifold, which we wish to endow with a Liouville structure. 4 As mentioned above, the action of X‚ąó(T ) on MŌą does not preserve the Liouville form őĽ, and hence the latter does not descend to the quotient. One can instead try to deform őĽ to something X‚ąó(T )-invariant as follows. Suppose we are given a real-valued function h : MŌą ‚Üí R, such that for all ŌÉ ‚ąą X‚ąó(T ) we have ŌÉ‚ąódh = dh + őłŌÉ . Here őłŌÉ = őĻVŌÉ ŌČ

and VŌÉ is the vector field generating the action of Re (C‚ąó) defined by ŌÉ.Then őĽh = őĽ + df will be a X‚ąó(T )-invariant Liouville form, which descends to YŌą . One should further require that the associated isotopy of Liouville vector fields preserves őõ Ōą and dilates AŌą . The result would then be a Liouville manifold ( YŌą , őĽ h) whose Fukaya category can be locally modelled by őľSh őõŌą (MŌą , őĽ ). We do not at present know how to find such a function h. However, its existence would follow from the existence of a suitable hyperk¬® ahler structure on X by the same construction as in [28]. In this case, one

6. The category DŌą, G

In this section we study the category DŌą, G that carries commuting actions of H‚ąě and the Satake category Hsph 0 . We determine the structure of DŌą, G as module categories under both. The actions on

As a byproduct, we construct a fiber functor on the Satake category using microstalks, categorifying an old result of Evans and Mirkovic [22]. 6.6. Microlocal fiber functor for the Satake category. The focus of this subsection is the Satake category Hsph 0 itself. We give an interpretation of the functor (6.18) as a microstalk functor on the affine Grassmannian. The main result in this subsection are not used elsewhere in the paper but we believe it is of independent interest. However, making it into a rigorous argument involves some subtleties of homotopical algebra, including a homotopy version of compatibilities of (8.1), (8.3) with the action of the monoidal categories on the module categories and so forth. The argument below follows that general idea, but instead of considering the tensor product of homotopy categories we reduce the construction to tensor product of additive categories of projective objects in relevant abelian categories which is quite close to the familiar tensor product of rings over a given commutative ring. The reduction is achieved by invoking Koszul duality; as a byproduct of this approach we get a stronger statement involving an equivalence of abelian categories. 8.2. where the latter follows from the equivalence Db(A‚ąímod) ‚ąľ= Db(Coh( fg‚ą®)) by base change, along with their Gm equivariant versions. It remains to show that projective graded ( Gm-equivariant) A0 modules are sent into semisimple complexes of ¬ĮA-modules (i.e. a sum of simple modules and their homological shifts). One such projective module P0 corresponds to the structure sheaf of fg‚ą® √óg‚ą® {0}. Its image under Koszul duality is i‚ąó(O) where i : B‚ą® ‚Üí N ‚ą® is the zero section. This object corresponds to an irreducible ¬ĮA-module. Other projective modules P0 are obtained from P0 by geometric reflection functors [16], thus we are reduced to checking that the Koszul dual functors in the sense of [39] correspond to semi-simple endofunctors of Db( ¬ĮA‚ąímod Gm ). For a base field of large positive characteristic the latter is shown in [46]. The present case of a characteristic zero base field follows. The first equivalence in part (3) is [15, Corollary 6.3], while the second one is the main result of Lusztig‚Äôs program. See overview in the introduction to [2]; the main result of [2] provides an alternative proof. The composed equivalence between the first and the third category in part (3) is easily checked to be compatible with the natural Rep( G‚ą®) action. Using the description of modules over the small quantum group as Rep( G‚ą®) eigenobjects in representations of U Lus q [3] we get compatible equivalences in part (2). ‚Ė°

Appendix A. Specialization and microlocalization 

In this appendix we review the Kashiwara-Schapira microlocalization construction in the algebro-geometric context over an algebraically closed field of any characteristic. We also prove formulas for computing the specialization and microlocalization in the situation with a contracting Gm-action. A.1. Specialization.
